France</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Date</th><td class="infobox-data note">11 February to 16 July 1858</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Witness</th><td class="infobox-data note"><a href="/wiki/Bernadette_Soubirous" title="Bernadette Soubirous">Saint Bernadette Soubirous</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Type</th><td href="/wiki/Sanctuary_of_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes" title="Sanctuary of Our Lady of Lourdes">Sanctuary of Our Lady of Lourdes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lourdes,_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Lourdes, France">Lourdes, France</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Patronage</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Lourdes,_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Lourdes, France">Lourdes, France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quezon_City" title="Quezon City">Quezon City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tagaytay" title="Tagaytay">Tagaytay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Daegu" title="Daegu">Daegu</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Lancaster" class="mw-redirect" title="Diocese of Lancaster">Diocese of Lancaster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lourdes_School_of_Mandaluyong" class="mw-redirect" title="Lourdes School of Mandaluyong">Lourdes School of Mandaluyong</a>, bodily ills, sick people, asthmatics, protection from diseases</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Feast day</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/11_February" class="mw-redirect" title="11 February">11 February</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Our Lady of Lourdes</b> (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Notre-Dame de Lourdes</i>; <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">Occitan</a>: <i lang="oc">N\xc3\xb2stra Senhora de Lorda</i>) is a title of the <a href="/wiki/Mary,_mother_of_Jesus" title="Mary, mother of Jesus">Virgin Mary</a>. She is venerated under this title by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a> due to her <a href="/wiki/Lourdes_apparitions" title="Lourdes apparitions">apparitions</a> that occurred in <a href="/wiki/Lourdes" title="Lourdes">Lourdes</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>. The first apparition of 11 February 1858, of which <a href="/wiki/Bernadette_Soubirous" title="Bernadette Soubirous">Bernadette Soubirous</a> (age 14) told her mother that a "Lady" spoke to her in the cave of Massabielle (1.5 kilometres (0.93&#160;mi) from the town) while she was gathering firewood with her sister and a friend.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Similar apparitions of the "Lady" were reported on 18 occasions that year, until the climax revelation in which she introduced herself as: "the <a href="/wiki/Immaculate_Conception" title="Immaculate Conception">Immaculate Conception</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On 18 January 1862, the local Bishop of Tarbes Bertrand-S\xc3\xa9v\xc3\xa8re Laurence endorsed the veneration of the <a href="/wiki/Blessed_Virgin_Mary_(Roman_Catholic)" class="mw-redirect" title="Blessed Virgin Mary (Roman Catholic)">Blessed Virgin Mary</a> in Lourdes.\n</p><p>On 1 February 1876, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_IX" title="Pope Pius IX">Pope Pius IX</a> officially granted a decree of <a href="/wiki/Canonical_coronation" title="Canonical coronation">canonical coronation</a> to the image as <i>Notre-Dame du Saint Rosaire</i>. The coronation was performed by Cardinal <a href="/wiki/Pier_Francesco_Meglia" title="Pier Francesco Meglia">Pier Francesco Meglia</a> at the courtyard of what is now part of the <a href="/wiki/Rosary_Basilica" title="Rosary Basilica">Rosary Basilica</a> on 3 July 1876.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The image of Our Lady of Lourdes has been widely copied and reproduced in shrines and homes, often in <a href="/wiki/Garden" title="Garden">garden</a> landscapes. Bernadette Soubirous was canonized by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_XI" title="Pope Pius XI">Pope Pius XI</a> in 1933.<sup id="cite_ref-Burke850_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burke850-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Marian devotion has since steadily increased as ecclesiastical investigations sanctioned her visions. In later years, a large church was built at the site that has since<sup id="cite_ref-James317_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-James317-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> become a major site of religious pilgrimage.\n</p>\n<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Apparitions">Apparitions</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Our_Lady_of_Lourdes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Apparitions"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lourdes_apparitions" title="Lourdes apparitions">Lourdes apparitions</a></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bernadette_Soubirous" title="Bernadette Soubirous">Bernadette Soubirous</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Bernadette_Soubirous.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Bernadette_Soubirous.jpg/170px-Bernadette_Soubirous.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="217" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Bernadette_Soubirous.jpg/255px-Bernadette_Soubirous.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Bernadette_Soubirous.jpg/340px-Bernadette_Soubirous.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1291" data-file-height="1650" /></a><figcaption>Studio photograph of Bernadette Soubirous (age 14) in daily attire. (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;1 January 1858</span>)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>On 11 February 1858, Soubirous went with her sister Toinette and neighbor Jeanne Abadie to collect some firewood. While taking off her shoes and stockings to wade through the water near the <a href="/wiki/Grotto" title="Grotto">Grotto</a> of Massabielle, she said she heard the sound of two gusts of wind (<span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr">coups de vent</i></span>) but the trees and bushes nearby did not move. A wild rose in a natural niche in the grotto, however, did move.\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1244412712">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 32px}.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;margin-top:0}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{padding-left:1.6em}}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>I came back towards the grotto and started taking off my stockings. I had hardly taken off the first stocking when I heard a sound like a gust of wind. Then I turned my head towards the meadow. I saw the trees quite still: I went on taking off my stockings. I heard the same sound again. As I raised my head to look at the grotto, I saw a lady dressed in white, wearing a white dress, a blue girdle and a yellow rose on each foot, the same color as the chain of her rosary; the beads of the rosary were white \xe2\x80\xa6 From the niche, or rather the dark alcove behind it, came a dazzling light.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgilio_Tojetti_1877_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Virgilio_Tojetti_1877_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes.jpg/170px-Virgilio_Tojetti_1877_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="198" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Virgilio_Tojetti_1877_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes.jpg/255px-Virgilio_Tojetti_1877_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Virgilio_Tojetti_1877_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes.jpg/340px-Virgilio_Tojetti_1877_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="825" data-file-height="960" /></a><figcaption>Painting of the apparition of the Virgin Mary to Bernadette Soubirous in the Grotto at Massabielle, near <a href="/wiki/Lourdes,_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Lourdes, France">Lourdes, France</a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Soubirous tried to make the <a href="/wiki/Sign_of_the_cross" title="Sign of the cross">sign of the cross</a> but could not, as her hands were trembling. The lady smiled, and invited Soubirous to pray the rosary with her.<sup id="cite_ref-SHMI_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SHMI-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Soubirous tried to keep this a secret, but Toinette told her mother. After parental cross-examination, she and her sister received <a href="/wiki/Corporal_punishment" title="Corporal punishment">corporal punishment</a> for their story.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaurentin1988161_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaurentin1988161-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Three days later, 14 February, Soubirous returned to the grotto. She had brought holy water as a test that the apparition was not of evil origin/provenance: "The second time was the following Sunday \xe2\x80\xa6 Then I started to throw holy water in her direction, and at the same time I said that if she came from God she was to stay, but if not, she must go. She started to smile, and bowed ... This was the second time."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris19994_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris19994-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Soubirous\' companions are said to have become afraid when they saw her in ecstasy. She remained ecstatic even as they returned to the village. On 18 February, she spoke of being told by the Lady to return to the Grotto over a period of two weeks. She quoted the apparition: "The Lady only spoke to me the third time \xe2\x80\xa6 She told me also that she did not promise to make me happy in this world, but in the next."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaurentin1988161_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaurentin1988161-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Soubirous was ordered by her parents to never go there again. She went anyway, and on 24 February, Soubirous related that the apparition asked for prayer and penitence for the conversion of sinners.\n</p><p>The next day, she said the apparition asked her to dig in the ground and drink from the spring she found there. This made her dishevelled and some of her supporters were dismayed, but this act revealed the stream that soon became a focal point for pilgrimages.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris19997_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris19997-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Although it was muddy at first, the stream became increasingly clean. As word spread, this water was given to medical patients of all kinds, and many reports of miraculous cures followed. Seven of these cures were confirmed as lacking any medical explanations by Professor Verges in 1860. The first person with a "certified miracle" was a woman whose right hand had been deformed as a consequence of an accident. The government fenced off the grotto and issued stiff penalties for anybody trying to get near the off-limits area. In the process, Lourdes became a national issue in France, resulting in the intervention of Emperor <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_III" title="Napoleon III">Napoleon III</a> with an order to reopen the grotto on 4 October 1858. The church had decided to stay away from the controversy altogether.\n</p><p>Soubirous, knowing the local area well, managed to visit the barricaded grotto under cover of darkness. There, on 25&#160;March, she said she was told: "I am the <a href="/wiki/Immaculate_Conception" title="Immaculate Conception">Immaculate Conception</a>" (<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">"que soy era immaculada concepciou"</i></span>). On Easter Sunday, 7&#160;April, her examining doctor stated that Soubirous, in ecstasy, was observed to have held her hands over a lit candle without sustaining harm. On 16 July, Soubirous went for the last time to the grotto. "I have never seen her so beautiful before," she reported.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaurentin1988162_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaurentin1988162-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Statue_de_Notre_Dame_de_Lourdes.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Statue_de_Notre_Dame_de_Lourdes.jpg/220px-Statue_de_Notre_Dame_de_Lourdes.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="313" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Statue_de_Notre_Dame_de_Lourdes.jpg/330px-Statue_de_Notre_Dame_de_Lourdes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/30/Statue_de_Notre_Dame_de_Lourdes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="377" data-file-height="536" /></a><figcaption>The venerated image of Our Lady of Lourdes was granted a decree of <a href="/wiki/Canonical_coronation" title="Canonical coronation">canonical coronation</a> on 1 February 1876 by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_IX" title="Pope Pius IX">Pope Pius IX</a>. The coronation ceremony was executed on 3 July 1876. During that same year, an oversized golden <a href="/wiki/Laurel_wreath" title="Laurel wreath">laurel wreath</a> was placed at the base as well as a stellar halo being attached to the head of the image; both no longer present.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The Catholic Church, faced with nationwide questions, decided to institute an investigative commission on 17 November 1858. On 18 January 1860, the local bishop finally declared that: "The Virgin Mary did appear indeed to Bernadette Soubirous."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaurentin1988162_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaurentin1988162-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These events established the Marian veneration in Lourdes, which together with <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_F%C3%A1tima" title="Our Lady of F\xc3\xa1tima">F\xc3\xa1tima</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_Our_Lady_of_Guadalupe" title="Basilica of Our Lady of Guadalupe">Basilica of Our Lady of Guadalupe</a> is one of the most frequented Marian shrines in the world, and to which between 4 and 6 million pilgrims travel annually.\n</p><p>In 1863, <a href="/wiki/Joseph-Hugues_Fabisch" title="Joseph-Hugues Fabisch">Joseph-Hugues Fabisch</a> was charged to create a statue of the Virgin according to Soubirous\'s description. The work was placed in the grotto and solemnly dedicated on 4 April 1864 in presence of 20,000 pilgrims.\n</p><p>The veracity of the apparitions of Lourdes is not an article of faith for Catholics. Nevertheless, all recent popes have visited the Marian shrine at some time. <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XV" title="Pope Benedict XV">Benedict XV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_XI" title="Pope Pius XI">Pius XI</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_XXIII" title="Pope John XXIII">John XXIII</a> went there as bishops, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_XII" title="Pope Pius XII">Pius XII</a> as papal delegate. He also issued an <a href="/wiki/Encyclical" title="Encyclical">encyclical</a>, <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr"><a href="/wiki/Le_p%C3%A8lerinage_de_Lourdes" title="Le p\xc3\xa8lerinage de Lourdes">Le p\xc3\xa8lerinage de Lourdes</a></i></span>, on the one-hundredth anniversary of the apparitions in 1958. <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">John Paul II</a> visited Lourdes three times during his pontificate, and twice before as a bishop.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Bernadette\'s_description_of_Mary"><span id="Bernadette.27s_description_of_Mary"></span>Bernadette\'s description of Mary</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Our_Lady_of_Lourdes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Bernadette&#039;s description of Mary"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Soubirous described the apparition as a <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr">jeune fille</i></span> ("young girl") of about 14-15 years old; Soubirous insisted that the apparition was no taller than herself. At 1.40 metres (4&#160;ft 7&#160;in) tall, Soubirous was diminutive even by the standards of other poorly-nourished children.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris199972_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris199972-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Soubirous described the apparition as dressed in a flowing white robe, with a blue sash around her waist. This was the uniform of a religious group called the <a href="/wiki/Children_of_Mary" class="mw-redirect" title="Children of Mary">Children of Mary</a>, which, on account of her poverty, Soubirous was not permitted to join (although she was admitted after the apparitions).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris199943_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris199943-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Her aunt Bernarde was a long-time member.\n</p><p>The statue that currently stands in the niche within the grotto of Massabielle was created by the <a href="/wiki/Lyon" title="Lyon">Lyonnais</a> sculptor <a href="/wiki/Joseph-Hugues_Fabisch" title="Joseph-Hugues Fabisch">Joseph-Hugues Fabisch</a> in 1864. Although it has become an iconographic symbol of Our Lady of Lourdes, it depicts a figure which is not only older and taller than Soubirous\' description, but also more in keeping with orthodox and traditional representations of the Virgin Mary. On seeing the statue, Soubirous was profoundly disappointed with this representation of her vision.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Similar_events">Similar events</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Our_Lady_of_Lourdes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Similar events"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Antonio_Ciseri,_Apparizione_della_madonna_a_bernadette_di_lourdes,_1879,_01.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Antonio_Ciseri%2C_Apparizione_della_madonna_a_bernadette_di_lourdes%2C_1879%2C_01.jpg/170px-Antonio_Ciseri%2C_Apparizione_della_madonna_a_bernadette_di_lourdes%2C_1879%2C_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="264" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Antonio_Ciseri%2C_Apparizione_della_madonna_a_bernadette_di_lourdes%2C_1879%2C_01.jpg/255px-Antonio_Ciseri%2C_Apparizione_della_madonna_a_bernadette_di_lourdes%2C_1879%2C_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Antonio_Ciseri%2C_Apparizione_della_madonna_a_bernadette_di_lourdes%2C_1879%2C_01.jpg/340px-Antonio_Ciseri%2C_Apparizione_della_madonna_a_bernadette_di_lourdes%2C_1879%2C_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2544" data-file-height="3952" /></a><figcaption><i>Apparition of Our Lady of Lourdes to Bernadette</i> by <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Ciseri" title="Antonio Ciseri">Antonio Ciseri</a>, 1879</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In nearby <a href="/wiki/Lestelle-B%C3%A9tharram" title="Lestelle-B\xc3\xa9tharram">Lestelle-B\xc3\xa9tharram</a>, only a few kilometres from Lourdes, some shepherds guarding their flocks in the mountains observed a vision of a ray of light that guided them to the discovery of a statue of the Virgin Mary. Two attempts were made to remove the statue to a more prominent position; each time it disappeared and returned to its original location, at which a small chapel was built for it.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris199939_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris199939-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In the early 16th century, a 12-year-old shepherdess called Angl\xc3\xa8ze de Sagazan received a vision of the Virgin Mary near the spring at Garaison (part of the <a href="/wiki/Commune_in_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Commune in France">commune</a> of <a href="/wiki/Monl%C3%A9on-Magnoac" title="Monl\xc3\xa9on-Magnoac">Monl\xc3\xa9on-Magnoac</a>), somewhat further away. Angl\xc3\xa8ze\'s story is strikingly similar to that of Soubirous: she was a pious but illiterate and poorly educated girl, extremely impoverished, who spoke only in the local language, Gascon Occitan, but successfully convinced authorities that her vision was genuine and persuaded them to obey the instructions of her apparitions. Like Soubirous, she was the only one who could see the apparition (others could apparently hear it); however, the apparition at Garaison\'s supernatural powers tended toward the miraculous provision of abundant food, rather than healing the sick and injured. Mid-nineteenth century commentators noted the parallels between the events at Massabielle and Garaison, and interpreted the similarities as proof of the divine nature of Soubirous\' claims.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris199941_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris199941-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> At the time of Soubirous, Garaison was a noted center of pilgrimage and Marian devotion.\n</p><p>There are also several similarities between the <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_La_Salette" title="Our Lady of La Salette">apparition at La Salette</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Grenoble" title="Grenoble">Grenoble</a>, and Lourdes. La Salette is many hundreds of kilometres from Lourdes, and the events at La Salette predate those in Lourdes by 12 years. However, the Marian apparition at La Salette was tall and maternal (not petite and gentle like her Lourdes apparition) and had a darker, more threatening series of messages. It is not certain if Soubirous was aware of the events at La Salette.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarris199960_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarris199960-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Approval_by_a_local_bishop">Approval by a local bishop</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Our_Lady_of_Lourdes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Approval by a local bishop"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>On 18 January 1862, the <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Tarbes" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop of Tarbes">Bishop of Tarbes</a> Betrand Severt Laurence declared the following regarding the Marian apparitions:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1244412712"><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>"We are inspired by the Commission comprising wise, holy, learned and experienced priests who questioned the child, studied the facts, examined everything and weighed all the evidence. We have also called on science, and we remain convinced that the Apparitions are supernatural and divine, and that by consequence, what Soubirous saw was the Most Blessed Virgin. Our convictions are based on the testimony of Soubirous, but above all on the things that have happened, things which can be nothing other than divine intervention."<sup id="cite_ref-encounters_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encounters-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Lourdes_Basilique_et_gave.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Lourdes_Basilique_et_gave.jpg/220px-Lourdes_Basilique_et_gave.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Lourdes_Basilique_et_gave.jpg/330px-Lourdes_Basilique_et_gave.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Lourdes_Basilique_et_gave.jpg/440px-Lourdes_Basilique_et_gave.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2738" data-file-height="1906" /></a><figcaption>The sanctuary basilica built at <a href="/wiki/Lourdes" title="Lourdes">Lourdes</a> directly above the grotto of the apparitions</figcaption></figure>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Pontifical_approbations">Pontifical approbations</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Our_Lady_of_Lourdes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Pontifical approbations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:JPII_Lourdes.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/JPII_Lourdes.jpg/220px-JPII_Lourdes.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/JPII_Lourdes.jpg/330px-JPII_Lourdes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/JPII_Lourdes.jpg/440px-JPII_Lourdes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="534" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a> in 1983 at the Grotto of Massabielle of the Lourdes Shrine.</figcaption></figure>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Pope_Benedict_XVI_placing_a_novelty_crown_on_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes_on_occasion_for_the_sick_pilgrims,_11_February_2007.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Pope_Benedict_XVI_placing_a_novelty_crown_on_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes_on_occasion_for_the_sick_pilgrims%2C_11_February_2007.jpg/220px-Pope_Benedict_XVI_placing_a_novelty_crown_on_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes_on_occasion_for_the_sick_pilgrims%2C_11_February_2007.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Pope_Benedict_XVI_placing_a_novelty_crown_on_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes_on_occasion_for_the_sick_pilgrims%2C_11_February_2007.jpg/330px-Pope_Benedict_XVI_placing_a_novelty_crown_on_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes_on_occasion_for_the_sick_pilgrims%2C_11_February_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Pope_Benedict_XVI_placing_a_novelty_crown_on_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes_on_occasion_for_the_sick_pilgrims%2C_11_February_2007.jpg/440px-Pope_Benedict_XVI_placing_a_novelty_crown_on_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes_on_occasion_for_the_sick_pilgrims%2C_11_February_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2651" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Benedict XVI">Pope Benedict XVI</a> placing a crown<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>a<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> on Our Lady of Lourdes for the <a href="/wiki/Plenary_indulgence" class="mw-redirect" title="Plenary indulgence">plenary indulgence</a> he attached for pilgrims of the <a href="/wiki/World_Day_of_the_Sick" title="World Day of the Sick">World Day of the Sick</a>. 11 February 2007, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter%27s_Basilica" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Peter&#39;s Basilica">Saint Peter\'s Basilica</a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_IX" title="Pope Pius IX">Pope Pius IX</a> approved the veneration in Lourdes and supported the building of the Cathedral in 1870 to which he donated several gifts. He approved <a href="/wiki/Indulgences" class="mw-redirect" title="Indulgences">indulgences</a> and issued a canonical coronation to the courtyard image of the basilica on 1 February 1876. The coronation ceremony was performed by Cardinal Meglia on 3 July 1876.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pope_Leo_XIII" title="Pope Leo XIII">Pope Leo XIII</a> issued an apostolic letter <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">Parte Humanae Generi</i></span> in commemoration of the consecration of the new cathedral in Lourdes in 1879. He later issued a decree for a canonical coronation towards an image of Lourdes for <a href="/wiki/Pondicherry" title="Pondicherry">Pondicherry</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> on 21 February 1886. The rite of coronation was carried on 8 May 1886.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The same pontiff also made comparative remarks to the <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_Our_Lady_of_Brebi%C3%A8res" title="Basilica of Our Lady of Brebi\xc3\xa8res">Basilica of Our Lady of Brebi\xc3\xa8res</a> remarking it as "The Lourdes of the North" due to the influx of Marian pilgrims and miraculous claims of healings attached to the site.</li>\n<li>As <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Bologna" class="mw-redirect" title="Archbishop of Bologna">Archbishop of Bologna</a>, Archbishop <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XV" title="Pope Benedict XV">Giacomo della Chiesa</a> (the future <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XV" title="Pope Benedict XV">Pope Benedict XV</a>) organized a diocesan pilgrimage to Lourdes, requesting for Marian veneration in that area.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_X" title="Pope Pius X">Pope Pius X</a> in 1907 introduced the feast of the apparition of the Immaculate Virgin of Lourdes. In the same year he issued his encyclical <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la"><a href="/wiki/Pascendi_Dominici_gregis" title="Pascendi Dominici gregis">Pascendi Dominici gregis</a></i></span>, in which he specifically repeated the permission to venerate the virgin in Lourdes.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_XI" title="Pope Pius XI">Pope Pius XI</a> beatified the Marian visionary Bernadette Soubirous on 6 June 1925 and canonized her on the Feast of the Immaculate Conception on 8 December 1933 and determined her feast day to be 18 February.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Catholic_Pilgrims_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catholic_Pilgrims-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He later on 16 July 1934 issued a decree <i>Edocemur Admomum</i> confirming privileges of patronage for an image with the same namesake for the Church of Saint Martin in <a href="/wiki/Stella,_Liguria" title="Stella, Liguria">Stella, Liguria</a> in <a href="/wiki/Savona,_Italy" class="mw-redirect" title="Savona, Italy">Savona, Italy</a>. This document was signed by Cardinal <a href="/wiki/Eugenio_Pacelli" class="mw-redirect" title="Eugenio Pacelli">Eugenio Pacelli</a>. Later in 1937, the pope sent the same cardinal as his <a href="/wiki/Papal_legate" title="Papal legate">legate</a> to personally visit the sanctuary at Lourdes.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_XII" title="Pope Pius XII">Pope Pius XII</a> issued a papal encyclical <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr"><a href="/wiki/Le_p%C3%A8lerinage_de_Lourdes" title="Le p\xc3\xa8lerinage de Lourdes">Le p\xc3\xa8lerinage de Lourdes</a></i></span> on the 100th centenary anniversary of the Marian apparitions of Lourdes.</li>\n<li>As <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Milan" class="mw-redirect" title="Archbishop of Milan">Archbishop of Milan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Paul_VI" title="Pope Paul VI">Giovanni Battista Montini</a> (the future <a href="/wiki/Pope_Paul_VI" title="Pope Paul VI">Pope Paul VI</a>) visited Lourdes.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a> made three religious pilgrimages to Lourdes. He also instituted the <a href="/wiki/World_Day_of_the_Sick" title="World Day of the Sick">World Day of the Sick</a> in honor of Our Lady of Lourdes on 13 May 1992.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Benedict XVI">Pope Benedict XVI</a> issued a novelty coronation towards the Lourdes image on World Day of the Sick in 2007. In September 2008, he visited Lourdes commemorating the 150th anniversary of the Marian apparitions.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pope_Francis" title="Pope Francis">Pope Francis</a> granted a canonical coronation towards <a href="/wiki/National_Shrine_of_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes" title="National Shrine of Our Lady of Lourdes">a Lourdes image</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> on 5 September 2019. The coronation took place on 22 August 2020.</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Reported_healings">Reported healings</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Our_Lady_of_Lourdes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Reported healings"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lourdes_water" title="Lourdes water">Lourdes water</a></div>\n<p>The location of the spring was described to Soubirous by an apparition of Our Lady of Lourdes on 25 February 1858. Since that time many thousands of pilgrims to Lourdes have followed the instruction of Our Lady of Lourdes to "drink at the spring and wash in it".\n</p><p>Lourdes water has become a focus of devotion to the Virgin Mary at Lourdes. The Catholic Church has formally endorsed, although not dogmatic, for sick people to bathe and visit Lourdes for healing. Since the apparitions, many people have claimed to have been cured by drinking or bathing in it,<sup id="cite_ref-Ruth_Harris_1999,_p._312_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ruth_Harris_1999,_p._312-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the Lourdes authorities provide it free of charge to any who ask for it.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>An analysis of the water was commissioned by then mayor of Lourdes, Monsieur Anselme Lacad\xc3\xa9 in 1858. It was conducted by a professor in <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a>, who determined that the water was <a href="/wiki/Potable" class="mw-redirect" title="Potable">potable</a> and that it contained the following: oxygen, <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen" title="Nitrogen">nitrogen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carbonic_acid" title="Carbonic acid">carbonic acid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carbonates" class="mw-redirect" title="Carbonates">carbonates</a> of lime and magnesia, a trace of <a href="/wiki/Carbonate_of_iron" class="mw-redirect" title="Carbonate of iron">carbonate of iron</a>, an alkaline carbonate or silicate, <a href="/wiki/Chloride" title="Chloride">chlorides</a> of <a href="/wiki/Potassium" title="Potassium">potassium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sodium" title="Sodium">sodium</a>, traces of <a href="/wiki/Sulphates" class="mw-redirect" title="Sulphates">sulphates</a> of potassium and soda, traces of <a href="/wiki/Ammonia" title="Ammonia">ammonia</a>, and traces of <a href="/wiki/Iodine" title="Iodine">iodine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-civil_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-civil-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Essentially, the water is pure and inert. Lacad\xc3\xa9 had hoped that Lourdes water might have special mineral properties which would allow him to develop Lourdes into a spa town, to compete with neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Cauterets" title="Cauterets">Cauterets</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bagn%C3%A8res-de-Bigorre" title="Bagn\xc3\xa8res-de-Bigorre">Bagn\xc3\xa8res-de-Bigorre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ruth_Harris_1999,_p._312_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ruth_Harris_1999,_p._312-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="The_Lourdes_Medical_Bureau">The Lourdes Medical Bureau</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Our_Lady_of_Lourdes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: The Lourdes Medical Bureau"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lourdes_Medical_Bureau" title="Lourdes Medical Bureau">Lourdes Medical Bureau</a></div>\n<p>To ensure claims of cures were examined properly and to protect the town from fraudulent claims of miracles, the <a href="/wiki/Lourdes_Medical_Bureau" title="Lourdes Medical Bureau">Lourdes Medical Bureau</a> (Bureau Medical) was established at the request of <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_X" title="Pope Pius X">Pope Pius X</a>. It is completely under medical rather than ecclesiastical supervision. Approximately 7,500<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> people have sought to have their case confirmed as a miracle, of which 70<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> have been declared scientifically inexplicable by the bureau.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Sanctuary_of_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes">Sanctuary of Our Lady of Lourdes</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Our_Lady_of_Lourdes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Sanctuary of Our Lady of Lourdes"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sanctuary_of_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes" title="Sanctuary of Our Lady of Lourdes">Sanctuary of Our Lady of Lourdes</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Our_Lady_of_Lourdes_Basilica.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Our_Lady_of_Lourdes_Basilica.jpg/220px-Our_Lady_of_Lourdes_Basilica.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="210" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Our_Lady_of_Lourdes_Basilica.jpg/330px-Our_Lady_of_Lourdes_Basilica.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Our_Lady_of_Lourdes_Basilica.jpg/440px-Our_Lady_of_Lourdes_Basilica.jpg 2x" data-file-width="511" data-file-height="487" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Sanctuary_of_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes" title="Sanctuary of Our Lady of Lourdes">Sanctuary of Our Lady of Lourdes</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>The Sanctuary of Our Lady of Lourdes is a group of churches, religious buildings and <a href="/wiki/Place_of_worship" title="Place of worship">places of worship</a> on the site where the <a href="/wiki/Lourdes_apparitions" title="Lourdes apparitions">Lourdes apparitions</a> occurred in 1858, in the town of <a href="/wiki/Lourdes" title="Lourdes">Lourdes</a>, in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>. The area is owned and administered by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a> and is a destination for millions of pilgrims coming to venerate Our Lady of Lourdes. The sanctuary holds devotional activities, offices, and ensures accommodation for pilgrims with disabilities and those assisting them. The 52 <a href="/wiki/Hectare" title="Hectare">hectares</a> area of the sanctuary includes the grotto of Massabielle where <a href="/wiki/Bernadette_Soubirous" title="Bernadette Soubirous">Bernadette Soubirous</a> is said to have seen the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Mary" class="mw-redirect" title="Virgin Mary">Virgin Mary</a> and three basilicas, known as the <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_Our_Lady_of_the_Immaculate_Conception" title="Basilica of Our Lady of the Immaculate Conception">Upper Basilica</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Rosary_Basilica" title="Rosary Basilica">Lower Basilica</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_St._Pius_X" title="Basilica of St. Pius X">Underground Basilica</a>. It also includes a church, several chapels, a <a href="/wiki/Calvary_(sanctuary)" title="Calvary (sanctuary)">calvary</a> on a hill, an area of ground for gatherings, a square and alleys for processions, fountains providing <a href="/wiki/Lourdes_water" title="Lourdes water">Lourdes water</a> to pilgrims, baths for immersion in Lourdes water, residences for sick and disabled pilgrims, and the offices of the <a href="/wiki/Lourdes_Medical_Bureau" title="Lourdes Medical Bureau">Lourdes Medical Bureau</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The sanctuary is visited by millions each year, and Lourdes has become one of the prominent pilgrimage sites of the world. Large numbers of pilgrims travel to Lourdes each year in the hope of physical healing or spiritual renewal.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Other_places_of_veneration">Other places of veneration</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Our_Lady_of_Lourdes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Other places of veneration"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ballinasloe_St._Michael%27s_Church_South_Aisle_Fourth_Window_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes_and_Saint_Grellan_by_William_Earley_Detail_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes_and_Saint_Bernadette_2010_09_15.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Ballinasloe_St._Michael%27s_Church_South_Aisle_Fourth_Window_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes_and_Saint_Grellan_by_William_Earley_Detail_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes_and_Saint_Bernadette_2010_09_15.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="316" class="mw-file-element" href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai, India</a></li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Venerated_images_with_pontifical_decree">Venerated images with pontifical decree</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Our_Lady_of_Lourdes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Venerated images with pontifical decree"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Lourdeswiki.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Lourdeswiki.jpg/170px-Lourdeswiki.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="213" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Lourdeswiki.jpg/255px-Lourdeswiki.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Lourdeswiki.jpg/340px-Lourdeswiki.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="3000" /></a><figcaption>The venerated Marian image in Quezon City, canonically crowned by formal decree of <a href="/wiki/Pope_Francis" title="Pope Francis">Pope Francis</a> for the Philippines on 22 August 2020.</figcaption></figure>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_IX" title="Pope Pius IX">Pope Pius IX</a> granted a decree of coronation towards the image at the courtyard of the <a href="/wiki/Rosary_Basilica" title="Rosary Basilica">Rosary Basilica</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lourdes,_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Lourdes, France">Lourdes, France</a> on 1 February 1876.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pope_Leo_XIII" title="Pope Leo XIII">Pope Leo XIII</a> let the image of the high altar in the Shrine of Our Lady of Lourdes in <a href="/wiki/Pondicherry" title="Pondicherry">Pondicherry, India</a> crowned via decree on 21 February 1886.</li>\n<li>The image enshrined at the parish of Saint Martin in <a href="/wiki/Stella,_Liguria" title="Stella, Liguria">Stella, Savona</a>, Italy was crowned in July 1909; <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_XI" title="Pope Pius XI">Pope Pius XI</a> decreed that with special privileges on 16 July 1934.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/National_Shrine_of_Our_Lady_of_Lourdes" title="National Shrine of Our Lady of Lourdes">national image</a> in <a href="/wiki/Quezon_City" title="Quezon City">Quezon City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> was crowned by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Francis" title="Pope Francis">Pope Francis</a> via formal decree on 5 September 2019.</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Our_Lady_of_Lourdes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: In popular culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li>In 1941, the events became the basis of <a href="/wiki/Franz_Werfel" title="Franz Werfel">Franz Werfel</a>\'s best-selling novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Song_of_Bernadette_(novel)" title="The Song of Bernadette (novel)">The Song of Bernadette</a></i>. In <a href="/wiki/1943_in_film" title="1943 in film">1943</a>, the novel was filmed under <a href="/wiki/The_Song_of_Bernadette_(film)" title="The Song of Bernadette (film)">the same title</a>. <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Jones" title="Jennifer Jones">Jennifer Jones</a> played the title role while <a href="/wiki/Linda_Darnell" title="Linda Darnell">Linda Darnell</a> portrayed the Virgin Mary.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>In 1961 Dani\xc3\xa9le Ajoret portrayed Bernadette in <i>Bernadette of Lourdes</i> (French title: <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Il_suffit_d%27aimer&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Il suffit d&#39;aimer (page does not exist)">Il suffit d\'aimer</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Il_suffit_d%27aimer" class="extiw" title="fr:Il suffit d&#39;aimer">fr</a>&#93;</span></i> or <i>Love is Enough</i>) of <a href="/wiki/Robert_Dar%C3%A8ne" title="Robert Dar\xc3\xa8ne">Robert Dar\xc3\xa8ne</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>The 1997 book <i><a href="/wiki/The_Diving_Bell_and_the_Butterfly" title="The Diving Bell and the Butterfly">The Diving Bell and the Butterfly</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Jean-Dominique_Bauby" title="Jean-Dominique Bauby">Jean-Dominique Bauby</a> features a scene in which he and his girlfriend, Josephine, go to see Our Lady of Lourdes, known in the book as the <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(art)" title="Madonna (art)">Madonna</a>.</li>\n<li>The 2009 French feature film <i><a href="/wiki/Lourdes_(2009_film)" title="Lourdes (2009 film)">Lourdes</a></i> tells the story of wheelchair user Christine, who in order to escape her isolation, makes a life changing journey to Lourdes, the iconic site of pilgrimage in the <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenees</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><i>Lourdes</i>, 2019 documentary<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="See_also">See also</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Our_Lady_of_Lourdes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: See also"><span>edit</span></a><span p\xc3\xa8lerinage de Lourdes</a></i></span></li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Notes">Notes</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
